[        ]{.poetryoffset}even as boys, too sharp

[        ]{.poetryoffset}at the edges, although perhaps

[        ]{.poetryoffset}[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c13_r1.htm_page79}sometimes skillfully cut;

[        ]{.poetryoffset}we, like pieces of rock

[        ]{.poetryoffset}that have fallen on flowers.
:::

::: stanza
Flowers of the deeper soil,

loved by all roots,

you, Eurydice's sisters,

full of holy return

behind the ascending man.
:::

::: stanza
[        ]{.poetryoffset}We, afflicted by ourselves,

[        ]{.poetryoffset}gladly afflicting, gladly

[        ]{.poetryoffset}needing to be afflicted.

[        ]{.poetryoffset}We, who sleep with our anger

[        ]{.poetryoffset}laid beside us like a knife.
:::

::: stanza3
You, who are almost protection

where no one protects. The thought of you

is a shade-giving tree of sleep for the restless

creatures of a solitary man.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c13_r1.htm_nts-sect13a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect13){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_p03_r1.htm}

::: {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_p03_r1.htm_p03 .part}
# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_p03_r1.htm_page80}[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_p03_r1.htm_page81}*The Sonnets to Orpheus* {.part}

# *(1923)* {.part_title}

*Written as a grave-monument*

*for Vera Ouckama Knoop*

*Chateau de Muzot, February 1922*
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c14_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c14_r1.htm_page83}[FIRST PART](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c92_r1.htm){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c14_r1.htm_c14 .chapter}

------------------------------------------------------------------------

## [I](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c92_r1.htm_c92-s1){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c14_r1.htm_c14-s1 .section1}

::: stanza
A tree ascended there. Oh pure transcendence!

Oh Orpheus sings! Oh tall tree in the ear!

And all things hushed. Yet even in that silence

a new beginning, beckoning, change appeared.
:::

::: stanza
Creatures of stillness crowded from the bright

unbound forest, out of their lairs and nests;

and it was not from any dullness, not

from fear, that they were so quiet in themselves,
:::

::: stanza
but from just listening. Bellow, roar, shriek

seemed small inside their hearts. And where there had been

at most a makeshift hut to receive the music,
:::

::: stanza3
a shelter nailed up out of their darkest longing,

with an entryway that shuddered in the [wind---]{.nw}

you built a temple deep inside their hearing.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c14_r1.htm_nts-sect14a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect14){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c15_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c15_r1.htm_page85}[II](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c93_r1.htm){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c15_r1.htm_c15 .chapter}

::: stanza
And it was []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c15_r1.htm_c15-nts1}almost a girl and came to be

out of this single joy of song and lyre

and through her green veils shone forth radiantly

and made herself a bed inside my ear.
:::

::: stanza
And slept there. And her sleep was everything:

the awesome trees, the distances I had felt

so deeply that I could touch them, meadows in spring:

all wonders that had ever seized my heart.
:::

::: stanza
She slept the world. Singing god, how was that first

sleep so perfect that she had no desire

ever to wake? See: she arose and slept.
:::

::: stanza3
Where is her death now? Ah, will you discover

this theme before your song consumes [itself?---]{.nw}

Where is she vanishing? ... A girl almost....
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c15_r1.htm_nts-sect15a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect15){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c16_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c16_r1.htm_page87}[III](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c94_r1.htm){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c16_r1.htm_c16 .chapter}

::: stanza
A god can do it. But will you tell me how

a man can enter through the lyre's strings?

Our mind is split. And at the shadowed []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c16_r1.htm_c16-nts1}crossing

of heart-roads, there is no temple for Apollo.
:::

::: stanza
Song, as you have taught it, is not desire,

not wooing any grace that can be achieved;

song is reality. Simple, for a god.

But when can *we* be real? When does he pour
:::

::: stanza
the earth, the stars, into us? Young man,

it is not your loving, even if your mouth

was forced wide open by your own voice---learn
:::

::: stanza3
to forget that passionate music. It will end.

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c16_r1.htm_c16-nts2}True singing is a different breath, about

nothing. []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c16_r1.htm_c16-nts3}A gust inside the god. A wind.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c16_r1.htm_nts-sect16a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect16){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c17_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c17_r1.htm_page89}[IV](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c95_r1.htm){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c17_r1.htm_c17 .chapter}

::: stanza
O you tender ones, walk now and then

into the breath that blows coldly past.

Upon your cheeks let it tremble and part;

behind you it will tremble together again.
:::

::: stanza
O you blessèd ones, you who are whole,

you who seem the beginning of hearts,

bows for the arrows and arrows' [targets---]{.nw}

tear-bright, your lips more eternally smile.
:::

::: stanza
Don't be afraid to suffer; return

that heaviness to the earth's own weight;

heavy are the mountains, heavy the seas.
:::

::: stanza3
Even the small trees you planted as children

have long since become too heavy; you could not

carry them now. But the winds ... But the spaces ....
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c17_r1.htm_nts-sect17a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect17){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c18_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c18_r1.htm_page91}[V](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c96_r1.htm){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c18_r1.htm_c18 .chapter}

::: stanza
Erect no gravestone for him. Only this:

let the rose blossom each year for his sake.

For it *is* the god. His metamorphosis

in this and that. We do not need to look
:::

::: stanza
for other names. []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c18_r1.htm_c18-nts1}It is Orpheus once for all

whenever there is song. He comes and goes.

Isn't it enough if sometimes he can dwell

with us a few days longer than a rose?
:::

::: stanza
Though he himself is afraid to disappear,

he *has* to vanish: don't you understand?

The moment his word moves out beyond our life here,
:::

::: stanza3
he has gone where you will never find his trace.

The lyre's strings do not constrict his hands.

And it is in overstepping that he obeys.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c18_r1.htm_nts-sect18a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect18){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c19_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c19_r1.htm_page93}[VI](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c97_r1.htm){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c19_r1.htm_c19 .chapter}

::: stanza
Is he someone who dwells in this *single* world? No:

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c19_r1.htm_c19-nts1}both realms are the source of his earthly power.

He alone who has known the roots of the willow

can bend the []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c19_r1.htm_c19-nts2}willow-branch into a lyre.
:::

::: stanza
Overnight leave no bread on the table

and leave no milk: they draw back the [dead---.]{.nw}

But he, the conjuror, may he settle

under the calm of the eye's lowered lid
:::

::: stanza
to mix death into everything seen;

and may the magic of []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c19_r1.htm_c19-nts3}earthsmoke and rue

be as real to him as the clearest []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c19_r1.htm_c19-nts4}connection.
:::

::: stanza3
Nothing can trouble the dominance of

the true image. Whether from graves or from rooms,

let him praise finger-ring, bracelet, and jug.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c19_r1.htm_nts-sect19a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect19){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c20_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c20_r1.htm_page95}[VII](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c98_r1.htm){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c20_r1.htm_c20 .chapter}

::: stanza
Praising is what matters! He was summoned for that,

and came to us like the ore from a stone's

silence. His mortal heart presses out

a deathless, inexhaustible wine.
:::

::: stanza
Whenever he feels the god's paradigm grip

his throat, the voice does not die in his mouth.

All becomes vineyard, all becomes grape,

ripened on the hills of his sensuous South.
:::

::: stanza
Neither []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c20_r1.htm_c20-nts1}decay in the sepulcher of kings

nor any shadow fallen from the gods

can ever detract from his glorious praising.
:::

::: stanza3
For he is a herald who is with us always,

holding far into the doors of the dead

a bowl with ripe fruit worthy of praise.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c20_r1.htm_nts-sect20a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect20){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c21_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c21_r1.htm_page97}[VIII](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c99_r1.htm){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c21_r1.htm_c21 .chapter}

::: stanza
Only in the realm of Praising should Lament

walk, the naiad of the wept-for fountain,

watching over the stream of our complaint,

to keep it clear upon the very stone
:::

::: stanza
that bears the arch of triumph and the [altar.---]{.nw}

Look: around her shoulders dawns the bright

sense that she may be the youngest sister

among the deities hidden in our heart.
:::

::: stanza
Joy *knows*, and Longing has [accepted---]{.nw}

only Lament still learns; upon her beads,

night after night, she counts the ancient curse.
:::

::: stanza3
Yet awkward as she is, she suddenly

lifts a constellation of our voice,

glittering, into the pure nocturnal sky.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c21_r1.htm_nts-sect21a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect21){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c22_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c22_r1.htm_page99}[IX](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c100_r1.htm_c100){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c22_r1.htm_c22 .chapter}

::: stanza
Only he whose bright lyre

has sounded in shadows

may, looking onward, restore

his infinite praise.
:::

::: stanza
Only he who has eaten

poppies with the dead

will not lose ever again

the gentlest chord.
:::

::: stanza
Though the image upon the pool

often grows dim:

*Know and be still*.
:::

::: stanza3
Inside the Double World

all voices become

eternally mild.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c22_r1.htm_nts-sect22a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect22){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c23_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c23_r1.htm_page101}[X](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c101_r1.htm_c101){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c23_r1.htm_c23 .chapter}

::: stanza
You who are close to my heart always,

I welcome you, ancient []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c23_r1.htm_c23-nts1}coffins of stone,

which the cheerful water of Roman days

still flows through, like a wandering song.
:::

::: stanza
Or []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c23_r1.htm_c23-nts2}those other ones that are open wide

like the eyes of a happily waking []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c23_r1.htm_c23-nts3}shepherd

---with silence and []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c23_r1.htm_c23-nts4}bee-suck nettle inside,

from which ecstatic butterflies flittered;
:::

::: stanza
everything that has been wrestled from doubt

I welcome---the mouths that burst open after

long knowledge of what it is to be mute.
:::

::: stanza3
Do we know this, my friends, or don't we know this?

Both are formed by the hesitant hour

in the deep calm of the human face.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c23_r1.htm_nts-sect23a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect23){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c24_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c24_r1.htm_page103}[XI](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c102_r1.htm_c102){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c24_r1.htm_c24 .chapter}

::: stanza
Look at the sky. Are no two stars called []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c24_r1.htm_c24-nts1}"Rider"?

For this is printed strangely on us here:

this pride of earth. And look, the second figure

who drives and halts it: whom it has to bear.
:::

::: stanza
Aren't we, in our sinewy quintessence,

controlled like this, now raced and now reined in?

Path and turningpoint. Just a touch possesses.

New expanses. And the two are one.
:::

::: stanza
Or *are* they really? Don't both signify

the path they ride together now? But table

and pasture keep them separate, utterly.
:::

::: stanza3
Even the starry union is a fraud.

Yet gladly let us trust the valid symbol

for a moment. It is all we need.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c24_r1.htm_nts-sect24a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect24){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c25_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c25_r1.htm_page105}[XII](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c103_r1.htm_c103){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c25_r1.htm_c25 .chapter}

::: stanza
Hail to the god who joins us; for through him

arise the symbols where we truly live.

And, with tiny footsteps, the clocks move

separately from our authentic time.
:::

::: stanza
Though we are unaware of our true status,

our actions stem from pure relationship.

Far away, []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c25_r1.htm_c25-nts1}antennas hear antennas

and the empty distances transmit ...
:::

::: stanza
Pure readiness. Oh unheard starry music!

Isn't your sound protected from all static

by the ordinary business of our days?
:::

::: stanza3
In spite of all the farmer's work and worry,

he can't reach down to where the seed is slowly

transmuted into summer. The earth *bestows*.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c25_r1.htm_nts-sect25a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect25){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c26_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c26_r1.htm_page107}[XIII](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c104_r1.htm_c104){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c26_r1.htm_c26 .chapter}

::: stanza
Plump apple, smooth banana, melon, peach,

gooseberry ... How all this affluence

speaks death and life into the mouth ... I sense ...

Observe it from a child's transparent features
:::

::: stanza
while he tastes. This comes from far away.

What miracle is happening in your mouth?

Instead of words, discoveries flow out

from the ripe flesh, astonished to be free.
:::

::: stanza
Dare to say what []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c26_r1.htm_c26-nts1}"apple" truly is.

This sweetness that feels thick, dark, dense at first;

then, exquisitely lifted in your taste,
:::

::: stanza3
grows clarified, awake and luminous,

double-meaninged, sunny, earthy, [real---:]{.nw}

Oh knowledge, pleasure---inexhaustible.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c26_r1.htm_nts-sect26a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect26){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c27_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c27_r1.htm_page109}[XIV](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c105_r1.htm_c105){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c27_r1.htm_c27 .chapter}

::: stanza
We are involved with flower, leaf, and fruit.

They speak not just the language of one year.

From darkness a bright phenomenon appears

and still reflects, perhaps, the jealous glint
:::

::: stanza
of the dead, who fill the earth. How can we know

what part they play within the ancient cycle?

Long since, it has been their job to make the soil

vigorous with the force of their free marrow.
:::

::: stanza
But have they done it willingly? we ask ...

Does this fruit, formed by heavy slaves, push up

like a clenched fist, to threaten us, their masters?
:::

::: stanza3
Or in fact are *they* the masters, as they sleep

beside the roots and grant us, from their riches,

this hybrid Thing of speechless strength and kisses?
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c27_r1.htm_nts-sect27a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect27){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c28_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c28_r1.htm_page111}[XV](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c106_r1.htm_c106){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c28_r1.htm_c28 .chapter}

::: stanza
Wait ..., that tastes good ... But already it's gone.

.... A few notes of music, a tapping, a faint

hum---: you girls, so warm and so silent,

dance the taste of the fruit you have known!
:::

::: stanza
Dance the orange. Who can forget it,

drowning in itself, how it struggles through

against its own sweetness. You have possessed it.

Deliciously it has converted to you.
:::

::: stanza
Dance the orange. The sunnier [landscape---]{.nw}

fling it *from* you, allow it to shine

in the breeze of its homeland! Aglow, peel away
:::

::: stanza3
scent after scent. Create your own kinship

with the supple, gently reluctant rind

and the juice that fills it with succulent joy.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c28_r1.htm_nts-sect28a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect28){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c29_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c29_r1.htm_page113}[XVI](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c107_r1.htm_c107){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c29_r1.htm_c29 .chapter}

::: stanza
You are lonely, my friend, because you are....

*We*, with a word or a finger-sign,

gradually make the world our own,

though perhaps its weakest, most precarious part.
:::

::: stanza
How can fingers point out a [smell?---]{.nw}

Yet of the dark forces that lurk at our side

you feel many ... []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c29_r1.htm_c29-nts1}You know the dead,

and you shrink away from the magic spell.
:::

::: stanza
Look, we two together must bear

piecework and parts, as if they were

the whole. But be careful. Above all, []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c29_r1.htm_c29-nts2}don't plant
:::

::: stanza3
me inside your heart. I'd outgrow you. But I

will guide []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c29_r1.htm_c29-nts3}*my* master's hand and will say:

Here. This is Esau beneath his pelt.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c29_r1.htm_nts-sect29a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect29){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c30_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c30_r1.htm_page115}[XVII](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c108_r1.htm_c108){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c30_r1.htm_c30 .chapter}

::: stanza
At bottom the Ancient One, gnarled

root hidden deep,

origin unbeheld

by those who branched up.
:::

::: stanza
Helmet and horn of hunters,

grandfathers' truths,

men who betrayed their brothers,

women like lutes ...
:::

::: stanza
Branch upon branch crowds close,

none of them free....

Keep climbing higher ... higher ...
:::

::: stanza3
Still, though, they break. Yet this

top one bends finally

into a lyre.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c30_r1.htm_nts-sect30a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect30){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c31_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c31_r1.htm_page117}[XVIII](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c109_r1.htm_c109){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c31_r1.htm_c31 .chapter}

::: stanza
Master, do you hear the New

quiver and rumble?

Harbingers step forth who

blare their approval.
:::

::: stanza
Surely no ear is whole

amid this noise,

yet the machine-part still

asks for our praise.
:::

::: stanza
Look, the machine:

rears up and takes revenge,

brings us to crawl and cringe.
:::

::: stanza3
Since all its strength is from us,

let it, desireless,

serve and remain.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c31_r1.htm_nts-sect31a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect31){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c32_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c32_r1.htm_page119}[XIX](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c110_r1.htm_c110){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c32_r1.htm_c32 .chapter}

::: stanza
Though the world keeps changing its form

as fast as a cloud, still

what is accomplished falls home

to the Primeval.
:::

::: stanza
Over the change and the passing,

larger and freer,

soars your eternal song,

god with the lyre.
:::

::: stanza
Never has grief been possessed,

never has love been learned,

and what removes us in death
:::

::: stanza3
is not revealed.

Only the song through the land

hallows and heals.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c32_r1.htm_nts-sect32a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect32){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c33_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c33_r1.htm_page121}[XX](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c111_r1.htm_c111){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c33_r1.htm_c33 .chapter}

::: stanza
But Master, what gift shall I dedicate to you,

who taught all creatures their ears?

---My thoughts of an evening long ago,

it was springtime, in Russia---a horse ...
:::

::: stanza
He came bounding from the village, alone, white,

with a hobble attached to one leg,

to stay alone in the fields all night;

how the mane beat against his neck
:::

::: stanza
to the rhythm of his perfect joy, in that hindered

gallop across the meadow.

What leaping went on in his stallion-blood!
:::

::: stanza3
He felt the expanses, and oh!

He sang and he heard---your []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c33_r1.htm_c33-nts1}cycle of myths

was completed *in* him.

[                        ]{.poetryoffset}His image: my gift.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c33_r1.htm_nts-sect33a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect33){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c34_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c34_r1.htm_page123}[XXI](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c112_r1.htm_c112){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c34_r1.htm_c34 .chapter}

::: stanza
Spring has returned. The earth resembles

a little girl who has memorized

many poems.... For all the trouble

of her long learning, she wins the prize.
:::

::: stanza
Her teacher was strict. We loved the white

in the old man's beard and shaggy eyebrows.

Now, whatever we ask about

the blue and the green, she knows, she knows!
:::

::: stanza
Earth, overjoyed to be out on vacation,

play with the children. We long to catch up,

jubilant Earth. The happiest will win.
:::

::: stanza3
What her teacher taught her, the numberless Things,

and what lies hidden in stem and in deep

difficult root, she sings, she sings!
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c34_r1.htm_nts-sect34a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect34){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c35_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c35_r1.htm_page125}[XXII](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c113_r1.htm_c113){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c35_r1.htm_c35 .chapter}

::: stanza
We are the driving ones.

Ah, but the step of time:

think of it as a dream

in what forever remains.
:::

::: stanza
All that is hurrying

soon will be over with;

only what lasts can bring

us to the truth.
:::

::: stanza
Young men, don't put your trust

into the trials of flight,

into the hot and quick.
:::

::: stanza3
All things already rest:

darkness and morning light,

flower and book.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c35_r1.htm_nts-sect35a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect35){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c36_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c36_r1.htm_page127}[XXIII](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c114_r1.htm_c114){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c36_r1.htm_c36 .chapter}

::: stanza
Not till the day when flight

no longer for its own sake ascends

into the silent heavens

propelled by its self-conceit,
:::

::: stanza
so that, in luminous outlines,

as the tool that has come to power,

it can float, caressed by the winds,

streamlined, agile, and [sure---]{.nw}
:::

::: stanza
not till a pure destination

outweighs the boyish boast

of how much machines can do
:::

::: stanza3
will, overwhelmed with gain,

one to whom distance is close

*be* what alone he flew.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c36_r1.htm_nts-sect36a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect36){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c37_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c37_r1.htm_page129}[XXIV](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c115_r1.htm_c115){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c37_r1.htm_c37 .chapter}

::: stanza
Shall we reject our primordial friendship, the sublime

unwooing gods, because the steel that we keep

harshly bringing to hardness has never known [them---]{.nw}

or shall we suddenly look for them on a map?
:::

::: stanza
All these powerful friends, who withdraw the dead

from the reach of the senses, touch nowhere against our wheels.

We have moved our banquets, our baths and our festivals,

far away. And their messengers, long since outstripped by our speed,
:::

::: stanza
have vanished. Lonelier now, dependent on one another

utterly, though not knowing one another at all,

we no longer lay out each path as a lovely meander,
:::

::: stanza3
but straight ahead. Only in factories do the once-consecrate flames still

burn and lift up the always heavier hammers.

We, though, keep losing what small strength we have, like swimmers.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c37_r1.htm_nts-sect37a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect37){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c38_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c38_r1.htm_page131}[XXV](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c116_r1.htm_c116){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c38_r1.htm_c38 .chapter}

::: stanza
But you now, dear girl, whom I loved like a flower whose name

I didn't know, you who so early were taken away:

I will once more call up your image and show it to them,

beautiful companion of the unsubduable cry.
:::

::: stanza
Dancer whose body filled with your hesitant fate,

pausing, as though your young flesh had been cast in bronze;

grieving and listening---. Then, from the high dominions,

unearthly music fell into your altered heart.
:::

::: stanza
Already possessed by shadows, with illness near,

your blood flowed darkly; yet, though for a moment suspicious,

it burst out into the natural pulses of spring.
:::

::: stanza3
Again and again interrupted by downfall and darkness,

earthly, it gleamed. Till, after a terrible pounding,

it entered the inconsolably open door.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c38_r1.htm_nts-sect38a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect38){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c39_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c39_r1.htm_page133}[XXVI](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c117_r1.htm_c117){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c39_r1.htm_c39 .chapter}

::: stanza
But you, divine poet, you who sang on till the end

as the swarm of []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c39_r1.htm_c39-nts1}rejected maenads []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c39_r1.htm_c39-nts2}attacked you, shrieking,

you overpowered their noise with harmony, and

from pure destruction arose your transfigured song.
:::

::: stanza
Their hatred []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c39_r1.htm_c39-nts3}could not destroy your head or your lyre,

however they wrestled and raged; and each one of the sharp

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c39_r1.htm_c39-nts4}stones that they hurled, vengeance-crazed, at your heart

softened while it was in mid-flight, enchanted to hear.
:::

::: stanza
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c39_r1.htm_c39-nts5}At last they killed you and broke you in pieces while

your sound kept lingering on in lions and boulders,

in trees and in birds. There you are singing still.
:::

::: stanza3
Oh you lost god! You inexhaustible trace!

Only because you were torn and scattered through Nature

have *we* become hearers now and a rescuing voice.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c39_r1.htm_nts-sect39a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect39){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c40_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c40_r1.htm_page135}[SECOND PART](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c118_r1.htm_c118){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c40_r1.htm_c40 .chapter}

------------------------------------------------------------------------

## [I](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c118_r1.htm_c118-s1){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c40_r1.htm_c40-s1 .section1}

::: stanza
Breathing: you invisible poem! Complete

interchange of our own

essence with world-space. You counterweight

in which I rhythmically happen.
:::

::: stanza
Single wave-motion whose

gradual sea I am;

you, most inclusive of all our possible [seas---]{.nw}

space grown warm.
:::

::: stanza
How many regions in space have already been

inside me. There are winds that seem like

my wandering son.
:::

::: stanza3
Do you recognize me, air, full of places I once absorbed?

You who were the smooth bark,

roundness, and leaf of my words.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c40_r1.htm_nts-sect40a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect40){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c41_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c41_r1.htm_page137}[II](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c119_r1.htm_c119){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c41_r1.htm_c41 .chapter}

::: stanza
Just as the master's *genuine* brushstroke

is sometimes caught by a hurried page

that happens to be there: so mirrors will take

into themselves the pure smiling image
:::

::: stanza
of girls as they test the morning, [alone---]{.nw}

or under the gleam of devoted candles.

And into their faces, one by one,

later, just a reflection falls.
:::

::: stanza
*How much* was once gazed into the charred

slow-dying glow of a fireplace:

glances of life, irretrievable.
:::

::: stanza3
Who knows what losses the earth has suffered?

One who, with sounds chat nonetheless praise,

can sing the heart born into the whole.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c41_r1.htm_nts-sect41a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect41){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c42_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c42_r1.htm_page139}[III](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c120_r1.htm_c120){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c42_r1.htm_c42 .chapter}

::: stanza
Mirrors: no one has ever known how

to describe what you are in your inmost realm.

As if filled with nothing but sieve-holes, you

fathomless in-between spaces of time.
:::

::: stanza
You prodigals of the empty [chamber---]{.nw}

vast as forests, at the close of day ...

And the chandelier strides like a []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c42_r1.htm_c42-nts1}sixteen-pointer

through your unenterability.
:::

::: stanza
Sometimes you are full of painting. A few

seem to have walked straight into your [depths---]{.nw}

others, shyly, you sent on past you.
:::

::: stanza3
But the loveliest will stay---until, beyond,

into her all-absorbed cheeks she lets

Narcissus penetrate, bright and unbound.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c42_r1.htm_nts-sect42a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect42){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c43_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c43_r1.htm_page141}[IV](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c121_r1.htm_c121){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c43_r1.htm_c43 .chapter}

::: stanza
Oh this beast is the one that never was.

They didn't know that; unconcerned, they had

loved its grace, its walk, and how it stood

looking at them calmly, with clear eyes.
:::

::: stanza
It hadn't *been*. But from their love, a pure

beast arose. They always left it room.

And in that heart-space, radiant and bare,

it raised its head and hardly needed to
:::

::: stanza
exist. They fed it, not with any grain,

but always just with the thought that it might be.

And this assurance gave the beast so much power,
:::

::: stanza3
it grew a horn upon its brow. One horn.

Afterward it approached a virgin, [whitely---]{.nw}

and was, inside the mirror and in her.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c43_r1.htm_nts-sect43a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect43){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c44_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c44_r1.htm_page143}[V](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c122_r1.htm_c122){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c44_r1.htm_c44 .chapter}

::: stanza
Flower-muscle that slowly opens back

the anemone to another meadow-dawn,

until her womb can feel the polyphonic

light of the sonorous heavens pouring down;
:::

::: stanza
muscle of an infinite acceptance,

stretched within the silent blossom-star,

at times []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c44_r1.htm_c44-nts1}*so* overpowered with abundance

that sunset's signal for repose is bare-
:::

::: stanza
ly able to return your too far hurled-

back petals for the darkness to revive:

you, strength and purpose of how many worlds!
:::

::: stanza3
We violent ones remain a little longer.

Ah but *when*, in which of all our lives,

shall we at last be open and receivers?
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c44_r1.htm_nts-sect44a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect44){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c45_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c45_r1.htm_page145}[VI](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c123_r1.htm_c123){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c45_r1.htm_c45 .chapter}

::: stanza
Rose, you majesty---once, to the ancients, you were

just a calyx with the simplest of rims.

But for us, you are the full, the numberless flower,

the inexhaustible countenance.
:::

::: stanza
In your wealth you seem to be wearing gown upon gown

upon a body of nothing but light;

yet each separate petal is at the same time the negation

of all clothing and the refusal of it.
:::

::: stanza
Your fragrance has been calling its sweetest names

in our direction, for hundreds of years;

suddenly it hangs in the air like fame.
:::

::: stanza3
Even so, we have never known what to call it; we guess ...

And memory is filled with it unawares

which we prayed for from hours that belong to us.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c45_r1.htm_nts-sect45a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect45){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c46_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c46_r1.htm_page147}[VII](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c124_r1.htm_c124){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c46_r1.htm_c46 .chapter}

::: stanza
Flowers, you who are kin to the hands that arrange

(gentle girls' hands of present and past),

who often lay on the garden table, from edge

to edge, exhausted and slightly bruised,
:::

::: stanza
waiting for the water once more to bring you back whole

from the death that had just begun---and now

lifted again between the fast-streaming poles

of sensitive fingers that are able to do
:::

::: stanza
even more good than you guessed, as you lightly uncurled,

coming to yourselves again in the pitcher,

slowly cooling, and exhaling the warmth of girls
:::

::: stanza3
like long confessions, like dreary wearying sins

committed by being plucked, which once more

relate you to those who in blossoming are your cousins.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c46_r1.htm_nts-sect46a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect46){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c47_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c47_r1.htm_page149}[VIII](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c125_r1.htm_c125){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c47_r1.htm_c47 .chapter}

::: stanza
You playmates of mine in the scattered parks of the city,

small friends from a childhood of long ago:

how we found and liked one another, hesitantly,

and, like []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c47_r1.htm_c47-nts1}the lamb with the talking scroll,
:::

::: stanza
spoke with our silence. When we were filled with joy,

it belonged to no one: it was simply there.

And how it dissolved among all the adults who passed by

and in the fears of the endless year.
:::

::: stanza
Wheels rolled past us, we stood and stared at the carriages;

houses surrounded us, solid but untrue---and none

of them ever knew us. *What* in that world was real?
:::

::: stanza3
Nothing. Only the balls. Their magnificent arches.

Not even the children ... But sometimes one,

oh a vanishing one, stepped under the plummeting ball.
:::

*(In memoriam Egon von Rilke)*

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c47_r1.htm_nts-sect47a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect47){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c48_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c48_r1.htm_page151}[IX](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c126_r1.htm_c126){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c48_r1.htm_c48 .chapter}

::: stanza
Don't boast, you judges, that you have dispensed with torture

and that convicts are no longer shackled by the neck or heel.

No heart is enhanced, not one is---because a tender

spasm of mercy twists your mouths into a smile.
:::

::: stanza
What the scaffold received through the ages, it has given back

again, as children give back their battered old

birthday toys. Into the pure and lofty and gatelike

open heart he would differently enter, the god
:::

::: stanza
of true mercy. Sudden, huge, he would stride through and grip

us dazzled with radiance all around.

*More* than a wind for the massive confident ships.
:::

::: stanza3
And not any less transforming than the deep intuition

that wins us over without a sound

like a quietly playing child of an infinite union.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c48_r1.htm_nts-sect48a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect48){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c49_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c49_r1.htm_page153}[X](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c127_r1.htm_c127){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c49_r1.htm_c49 .chapter}

::: stanza
All we have gained the machine threatens, as long

as it dares to exist in the mind and not in obedience.

To dim the masterful hand's more glorious lingering,

for the determined structure it more rigidly cuts the stones.
:::

::: stanza
Nowhere does it stay behind; we cannot escape it at last

as it rules, self-guided, self-oiled, from its silent factory.

It thinks it is life: thinks it does everything best,

though with equal determination it can create or destroy.
:::

::: stanza
But still, existence for us is a miracle; in a hundred

places it is still the source. A playing of absolute

forces that no one can touch who has not knelt down in wonder.
:::

::: stanza3
Still there are words that can calmly approach the unsayable ...

And from the most tremulous stones music, forever new,

builds in unusable space her deified temple.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c49_r1.htm_nts-sect49a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect49){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c50_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c50_r1.htm_page155}[XI](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c128_r1.htm_c128){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c50_r1.htm_c50 .chapter}

::: stanza
Many calmly established rules of death have arisen,

ever-conquering man, since you acquired a taste

for hunting; yet more than all traps, I know you, sailcloths of linen

that used to be hung down into the caverns of []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c50_r1.htm_c50-nts1}Karst.
:::

::: stanza
Gently they lowered you in as if you were a signal

to celebrate peace. But then: the boy began shaking your side,

---and suddenly, from the caves, the darkness would fling out a handful

of pale doves into the day ...

[                ]{.poetryoffset}But even that is all right.
:::

::: stanza
Let every last twinge of pity be far from those who look [on---]{.nw}

far not just from the conscience of the vigilant, steadfast hunter

who fulfills what time has allowed.
:::

::: stanza3
*Killing too is a form of our ancient wandering affliction* ...

When the mind stays serene, whatever

happens to us is good.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c50_r1.htm_nts-sect50a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect50){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c51_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c51_r1.htm_page157}[XII](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c129_r1.htm_c129){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c51_r1.htm_c51 .chapter}

::: stanza
*Will* transformation. Oh be inspired for the flame

in which a Thing disappears and bursts into something else;

the spirit of re-creation which masters this earthly form

loves most the pivoting point where you are no longer yourself.
:::

::: stanza
What tightens into survival is already inert;

how safe is it really in its inconspicuous gray?

From far off a far greater hardness warns what is hard,

and the absent hammer is lifted high!
:::

::: stanza
He who pours himself out like a stream is acknowledged at last by Knowledge;

and she leads him enchanted through the harmonious country

that finishes often with starting, and with ending begins.
:::

::: stanza3
Every fortunate space that the two of them pass through, astonished,

is a child or grandchild of parting. And the transfigured []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c51_r1.htm_c51-nts1}Daphne,

as she feels herself become laurel, wants you to change into wind.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c51_r1.htm_nts-sect51a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect51){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c52_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c52_r1.htm_page159}[XIII](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c130_r1.htm_c130){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c52_r1.htm_c52 .chapter}

::: stanza
Be ahead of all parting, as though it already were

behind you, like the winter that has just gone by.

For among these winters there is one so endlessly winter

that only by wintering through it will your heart survive.
:::

::: stanza
Be forever dead in Eurydice---more gladly arise

into the seamless life proclaimed in your song.

Here, in the realm of decline, among momentary days,

be the crystal cup that shattered even as it rang.
:::

::: stanza
Be---and yet know the great void where all things begin,

the infinite source of your own most intense vibration,

so that, this once, you may give it your perfect assent.
:::

::: stanza3
To all that is used-up, and to all the muffled and dumb

creatures in the world's full reserve, the unsayable sums,

joyfully add your*self*, and []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c52_r1.htm_c52-nts1}cancel the count.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c52_r1.htm_nts-sect52a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect52){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c53_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c53_r1.htm_page161}[XIV](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c131_r1.htm_c131){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c53_r1.htm_c53 .chapter}

::: stanza
Look at the flowers, so faithful to what is earthly,

to whom we lend fate from the very border of fate.

And if they are sad about how they must wither and die,

perhaps it is our vocation to be their regret.
:::

::: stanza
All Things want to fly. Only *we* are weighed down by desire,

caught in ourselves and enthralled with our heaviness.

Oh what consuming, negative teachers we are

for them, while eternal childhood fills them with grace.
:::

::: stanza
If someone were to fall into intimate slumber, and slept

deeply with Things---: how easily he would come

to a different day, out of the mutual depth.
:::

::: stanza3
Or perhaps he would stay there; and they would blossom and praise

their newest convert, who now is like one of them,

all those silent companions in the wind of the meadows.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c53_r1.htm_nts-sect53a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect53){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c54_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c54_r1.htm_page163}[XV](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c132_r1.htm_c132){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c54_r1.htm_c54 .chapter}

::: stanza
O fountain-mouth, you generous, always-filled

mouth that speaks pure oneness, [constantly---]{.nw}

you marble mask before the water's still

flowing face. And in the background, the
:::

::: stanza
slow descent of aqueducts. From far

graves, and from the sloping Apennines,

they bring you all your syllables, which pour

down from your blackened, aging chin
:::

::: stanza
into the basin lying underneath.

This is the intimate and sleeping ear,

the marble ear, in which you always speak.
:::

::: stanza3
An ear of Earth. Just with herself alone

does she talk this way. And if a jug slips in,

she feels that you are interrupting her.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c54_r1.htm_nts-sect54a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect54){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c55_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c55_r1.htm_page165}[XVI](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c133_r1.htm_c133){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c55_r1.htm_c55 .chapter}

::: stanza
Over and over by us torn in two,

the god is the hidden place that heals again.

We are sharp-edged, because we want to know,

but he is always scattered and serene.
:::

::: stanza
Even the pure, the consecrated gift

he takes into his world no other way

than by positioning himself, unmoved,

to face the one end that is free.
:::

::: stanza
Only the dead may drink

from the source that we just hear, the unseen pool,

when the god, mute, allows them with a gesture.
:::

::: stanza3
Here, to us, only the noise is offered.

And the lamb keeps begging for its bell

because of a more quiet instinct.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c55_r1.htm_nts-sect55a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect55){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c56_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c56_r1.htm_page167}[XVII](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c134_r1.htm_c134){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c56_r1.htm_c56 .chapter}

::: stanza
Where, inside what forever blissfully watered gardens, upon what trees,

out of what deep and tenderly unpetaled flower-cups,

do the exotic fruits of consolation hang ripening? Those

rare delicacies, of which you find one perhaps
:::

::: stanza
in the trampled meadows of your poverty. Time and again

you have stood there marveling over the sheer size of the fruit,

over its wholeness, its smooth and unmottled skin,

and that the lightheaded bird or the jealous worm under the ground had not
:::

::: stanza
snatched it away from your hands. *Are* there such trees, flown through

by angels and so strangely cared for by gardeners hidden and slow

that they bear their fruit to nourish us, without being ours?
:::

::: stanza3
Is it true we have never been able (we who are only

shadows and shades), through our ripening and wilting so early,

to disturb the enormous calm of those patient summers?
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c56_r1.htm_nts-sect56a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect56){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c57_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c57_r1.htm_page169}[XVIII](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c135_r1.htm_c135){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c57_r1.htm_c57 .chapter}

::: stanza
Dancing girl: transformation

of all transience into steps: how you offered it there.

And the arm-raised whirl at the end, that tree made of motion,

didn't it fully possess the pivoted year?
:::

::: stanza
Didn't it, so that your previous swirling might swarm

in the midst of it, suddenly blossom with stillness? And above,

wasn't it sunshine, wasn't it summer, the warmth,

the pure, immeasurable warmth that you gave?
:::

::: stanza
But it bore fruit also, it bore fruit, your tree of bliss.

Aren't they here in their tranquil season: the jug,

whirling to ripeness, and the even more ripened vase?
:::

::: stanza3
And in the pictures: can't we still see the drawing

which your eyebrow's dark evanescent stroke

quickly inscribed on the surface of its own turning?
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c57_r1.htm_nts-sect57a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect57){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c58_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c58_r1.htm_page171}[XIX](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c136_r1.htm_c136){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c58_r1.htm_c58 .chapter}

::: stanza
Somewhere gold lives, luxurious, inside the pampering bank,

on intimate terms with thousands. Meanwhile, the wretched

blindman begging here seems, even to a penny, just like

some always-forgotten corner or the dustpile beneath a bed.
:::

::: stanza
In all the most elegant shops money is at ease

and steps out in shiny costumes of furs, carnations, and silks.

He, the silent one, stands in the narrow breath-pause

made by money breathing as it slumbers or wakes.
:::

::: stanza
Oh how can it close at night, that hand which is always open?

Tomorrow and each day Fate will arrive and hold it out: clear,

squalid, at any moment likely to be destroyed.
:::

::: stanza3
If only someone who could *see*, astonished at its long duration,

would understand it and praise it. Sayable only for the singer.

Audible only to the god.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c58_r1.htm_nts-sect58a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect58){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c59_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c59_r1.htm_page173}[XX](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c137_r1.htm_c137){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c59_r1.htm_c59 .chapter}

::: stanza
In between stars, what distances; and yet, how much vaster the distance

that we learn from what is right *here*.

Someone, for example a child ... and beside him, his brother or [sister---]{.nw}

oh how incomprehensibly far.
:::

::: stanza
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c59_r1.htm_c59-nts1}Fate measures us perhaps according to what is real,

so it seems to us not our own;

think of how vast a distance there is from the girl

to the loved and avoided man.
:::

::: stanza
All things are far---and nowhere does the circle close.

Look at the []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c59_r1.htm_c59-nts2}fish, served up on the gaily set table:

how peculiar its face on the dish.
:::

::: stanza3
All fish are mute ..., one used to think. But who knows?

Isn't there at last []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c59_r1.htm_c59-nts3}a place where, *without* them, we would be able

to speak in the language of fish?
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c59_r1.htm_nts-sect59a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect59){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c60_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c60_r1.htm_page175}[XXI](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c138_r1.htm_c138){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c60_r1.htm_c60 .chapter}

::: stanza
Sing of the gardens, my heart, that you never saw; as if glass

domes had been placed upon them, unreached forever.

Fountains and roses of []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c60_r1.htm_c60-nts1}Ispahan or [Shiraz---]{.nw}

sing of their happiness, praise them: unlike all others.
:::

::: stanza
Show that you always feel them, forever close.

That when their figs ripen, it is you they are ripening for.

That you know every breeze which, among the blossoms they bear,

is intensified till it almost becomes a face.
:::

::: stanza
Avoid the illusion that there can be any lack

for someone who wishes, then fully decides: to be!

Silken thread, you were woven into the fabric.
:::

::: stanza3
Whatever the design with which you are inwardly joined

(even for only one moment amid years of grief),

feel that the whole, the marvelous carpet is meant.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c60_r1.htm_nts-sect60a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect60){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c61_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c61_r1.htm_page177}[XXII](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c139_r1.htm_c139){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c61_r1.htm_c61 .chapter}

::: stanza
Oh in spite of fate: the glorious overflowings

of our existence, spouted upward in [parks---]{.nw}

or as stone-carved men who bear upon shoulders and backs

the weight overhead, braced on the sheer edge of buildings.
:::

::: stanza
Oh the bronze []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c61_r1.htm_c61-nts1}bell that, day after day, can lift

its club to shatter our dull quotidian hum.

Or the *only* presence, in []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c61_r1.htm_c61-nts2}Karnak, the column, the column

in which temples that were almost eternal have been outlived.
:::

::: stanza
For us these abundances plunge past, no longer central

but only appearing as haste, out of the horizontal

yellow day and into the overwhelmed, dazzled night.
:::

::: stanza3
But this frenzy too will subside, leaving no traces.

Arcs of airplanes and those who drove them through space,

none perhaps is in vain. Yet only as thought.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c61_r1.htm_nts-sect61a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect61){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c62_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c62_r1.htm_page179}[XXIII](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c140_r1.htm_c140){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c62_r1.htm_c62 .chapter}

::: stanza
Call me to the one among your moments

that stands against you, ineluctably:

intimate as []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c62_r1.htm_c62-nts1}a dog's imploring glance

but, again, forever, turned away
:::

::: stanza
when you think you've captured it at last.

What seems so far from you is most your own.

We are already free, and were dismissed

where we thought we soon would be at home.
:::

::: stanza
Anxious, we keep longing for a [foothold---]{.nw}

we, at times too young for what is old

and too old for what has never been;
:::

::: stanza3
doing justice only where we praise,

because we are the branch, the iron blade,

and sweet danger, ripening from within.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c62_r1.htm_nts-sect62a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect62){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c63_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c63_r1.htm_page181}[XXIV](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c141_r1.htm_c141){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c63_r1.htm_c63 .chapter}

::: stanza
Oh the delight, ever new, out of loosened soil!

The ones who first dared were almost without any help.

Nonetheless, at fortunate harbors, cities sprang up,

and pitchers were nonetheless filled with water and oil.
:::

::: stanza
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c63_r1.htm_c63-nts1}Gods: we project them first in the boldest of sketches,

which sullen Fate keeps crumpling and tossing away.

But for all that, the gods are immortal. Surely we may

hear out the one who, in the end, will hear us.
:::

::: stanza
We, one generation through thousands of lifetimes: women

and men, who are more and more filled with the child we will bear,

so that through it we may be shattered and overtaken.
:::

::: stanza3
We, the endlessly dared---how far we have come!

And only taciturn Death can know what we are

and how he must always profit when he lends us time.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c63_r1.htm_nts-sect63a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect63){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c64_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c64_r1.htm_page183}[XXV](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c142_r1.htm_c142){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c64_r1.htm_c64 .chapter}

::: stanza
Already (listen!) you can hear the first

harrows; once more the rhythm of men

through the held-back silence of the resolute earth

in early spring. What has so often
:::

::: stanza
come to you is coming once more,

vivid as if for the first time. Now,

slowly, you await what you always hoped for

but never took. It always took *you*.
:::

::: stanza
Even the leaves of wintered-through oaks

seem in the twilight a future brown.

Breezes signal, then signal back.
:::

::: stanza3
Black are the bushes. Yet heaps of dung

lie more intensely black on the ground.

Every hour that goes by grows younger.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c64_r1.htm_nts-sect64a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect64){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c65_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c65_r1.htm_page185}[XXVI](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c143_r1.htm_c143){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c65_r1.htm_c65 .chapter}

::: stanza
How deeply the cry of a bird can move us ...

*Any* cry that is cried out whole.

But children, playing in their open [space---]{.nw}

already their cries have become unreal.
:::

::: stanza
They cry out chance. And into the silent

seamless world, into which birds' cries

fully (as men into dream-space) blend,

they hammer the hard-edged wedge of their noise.
:::

::: stanza
Alas, where are we? Freer and freer,

like colored kites torn loose from their strings,

we toss half-high-up, framed by cold laughter,
:::

::: stanza3
slashed by the wind.---Oh compose the criers,

harmonious god! let them wake resounding,

let their clear stream carry the head and the lyre.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c65_r1.htm_nts-sect65a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect65){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c66_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c66_r1.htm_page187}[XXVII](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c144_r1.htm_c144){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c66_r1.htm_c66 .chapter}

::: stanza
Does it really exist, Time, the Destroyer?

When will it crush the fortress on the peaceful height?

This heart, which belongs to the infinite gods forever,

when will the []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c66_r1.htm_c66-nts1}Demiurge violate *it*?
:::

::: stanza
Are we really as fate keeps trying to convince us,

weak and brittle in an alien world?

And childhood, with all its divining voices,

is it later, down to its first root, stilled?
:::

::: stanza
Ah, the ghost of the transient

moves through the open, innocent

heart like a summer cloud.
:::

::: stanza3
As who we are, desperate, driving,

we still matter among the abiding

powers as a use of the gods.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c66_r1.htm_nts-sect66a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect66){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c67_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c67_r1.htm_page189}[XXVIII](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c145_r1.htm_c145){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c67_r1.htm_c67 .chapter}

::: stanza
Oh come and go. You, almost still a [child---]{.nw}

for just a moment fill out the dance-figure

into the constellation of those bold

dances in which dull, obsessive Nature
:::

::: stanza
is fleetingly surpassed. For she was stirred

to total hearing just when Orpheus sang.

You were still moved by those primeval words

and a bit surprised if any tree took long
:::

::: stanza
to step with you into the listening ear.

You knew the place where once the lyre arose

resounding: the unheard, unheard-of center.
:::

::: stanza3
For *its* sake you tried out your lovely motion

and hoped that you would one day turn your friend's

body toward the perfect celebration.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c67_r1.htm_nts-sect67a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect67){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c68_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c68_r1.htm_page191}[XXIX](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c146_r1.htm_c146){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c68_r1.htm_c68 .chapter}

::: stanza
Silent friend of many distances, feel

how your breath enlarges all of space.

Let your presence ring out []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c68_r1.htm_c68-nts1}like a bell

into the night. []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c68_r1.htm_c68-nts2}What feeds upon your face
:::

::: stanza
grows mighty from the nourishment thus offered.

Move through transformation, out and in.

What is the deepest loss that you have suffered?

If drinking is bitter, change yourself to wine.
:::

::: stanza
In this immeasurable darkness, be the power

that rounds your senses []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c68_r1.htm_c68-nts3}in their magic ring,

the sense of their mysterious encounter.
:::

::: stanza3
And if the earthly no longer knows your name,

whisper to the silent earth: I'm flowing.

To the flashing water say: I am.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c68_r1.htm_nts-sect68a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect68){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_p04_r1.htm}

::: {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_p04_r1.htm_p04 .part}
# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_p04_r1.htm_page192}[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_p04_r1.htm_page193}*Appendix to The Sonnets to Orpheus* {.part}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c69_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c69_r1.htm_page195}[\[I\]](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c147_r1.htm_c147){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c69_r1.htm_c69 .chapter}

::: stanza
Praising is what matters! He was summoned for that,

and came to us like the ore from a stone's

silence. His mortal heart presses out

a deathless, inexhaustible wine!
:::

::: stanza
Don't be confused if kings are discovered

rotting in their sepulchers, gnawed by the [worm---]{.nw}

for a while the decay of body and head

assailed him too with intense alarm;
:::

::: stanza
he, however, despising all doubt,

throttled the stench and with praise affirmed

the daily by day and the nightly at night,
:::

::: stanza3
for who knows what is transformed by the graces?

Kneeling from the maggots' marketplace,

he lifted the []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c69_r1.htm_c69-nts1}Golden Fleece, unharmed.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c69_r1.htm_nts-sect69a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect69){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c70_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c70_r1.htm_page197}[\[II\]](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c148_r1.htm_c148){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c70_r1.htm_c70 .chapter}

::: stanza
The New, my friends, is not a matter of

letting machines force out our handiwork.

Don't be confused by change; soon those who have

praised the "New" will realize their mistake.
:::

::: stanza
For look, the Whole is infinitely newer

than a cable or a high apartment house.

The stars keep blazing with an ancient fire,

and all more recent fires will fade out.
:::

::: stanza
Not even the longest, strongest of transmissions

can turn the wheels of what will be.

Across the moment, aeons speak with aeons.
:::

::: stanza3
*More* than we experienced has gone by.

And the future holds the most remote event

in union with what we most deeply want.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c70_r1.htm_nts-sect70a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect70){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c71_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c71_r1.htm_page199}[\[III\]](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c149_r1.htm_c149){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c71_r1.htm_c71 .chapter}

::: stanza
Brew us the magic in which all limits dissolve,

spirit forever bent to the fire!

That fathomless limit of evil, first, which revolves

also around those who are resting and do not stir.
:::

::: stanza
Dissolve with a few drops whatever excludes in the limit

of the ages, which makes our past wisdom a fraud;

for how deeply we have absorbed the Athenian sunlight

and the mystery of the Egyptian falcon or god.
:::

::: stanza
Don't rest until the boundary that keeps the sexes

in meaningless conflict has disappeared.

Open up childhood and the wombs of more truly expectant
:::

::: stanza3
generous mothers so that, shaming all that is empty,

and not confused by the hindering wood,

they may give birth to future rivers, augmenting the sea.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c71_r1.htm_nts-sect71a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect71){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c72_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c72_r1.htm_page201}[\[IV\]](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c150_r1.htm_c150){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c72_r1.htm_c72 .chapter}

::: stanza
Seek no more than what the []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c72_r1.htm_c72-nts1}stela knows,

and the mild image sculpted in the stone:

almost cheerfully, with a lightness, as

though they were exempt from earthly pain.
:::

::: stanza
Experience no further than the pure

direction in the world's withdrawing [stream---]{.nw}

ah, perhaps the icy jewels she wore

in that dimly lighted room.
:::

::: stanza
Be all the more consoled by what you see in

the elements that are most truly yours.

Wind consoles, and fire is consolation.
:::

::: stanza3
Here and There: you must be gripped by both,

strangely without a difference. Otherwise

you drain the whiteness from the whitest cloth.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c72_r1.htm_nts-sect72a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect72){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c73_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c73_r1.htm_page203}[\[V\]](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c151_r1.htm_c151){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c73_r1.htm_c73 .chapter}

::: stanza
Imagine: they might have experienced through each other

which of our miracles can be [shared---]{.nw}.

But while he gradually wrestled with growing older,

she was as yet unborn, a still-future child.
:::

::: stanza
*She*, perhaps---still playing with her friends, it was *she*

whom he had foreseen with boyish longing and love,

knowing the heart that would one day hold him completely;

and now a mere nothing parts them: a decade times five.
:::

::: stanza
Oh you bewildered god, you defrauded []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c73_r1.htm_c73-nts1}Hymen,

how sadly you extinguish the wedding-torch now

because it flung ashes onto that graying head.
:::

::: stanza3
Must he die in []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c73_r1.htm_c73-nts2}laments, and praise the beginning woman?

Or through his most silent yielding will he make her into

that unmoving form by which he is wholly exceeded?
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c73_r1.htm_nts-sect73a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect73){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c74_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c74_r1.htm_page205}[\[VI\]](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c152_r1.htm_c152){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c74_r1.htm_c74 .chapter}

::: stanza
When everything we create is far in spirit from the festive,

in the midst of our turbulent days let us think of what festivals *were*.

Look, they still play for us also, all of the []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c74_r1.htm_c74-nts1}Villa d'Este's

glittering fountains, though some are no longer towering there.
:::

::: stanza
Still, we are heirs to those gardens that poets once praised in their songs;

let us grasp our most urgent duty: to make them fully our own.

We perhaps are the last to be given such god-favored, fortunate Things,

their final chance to find an enduring home.
:::

::: stanza
Let not one god pass away. We all need each of them now,

let each be valid for us, each image formed in the depths.

Don't speak with the slightest disdain of whatever the heart can know.
:::

::: stanza3
Though we are no longer the ones for whom great festivals thrived,

this accomplishing fountain-jet that surges to us as strength

has traveled through aqueducts---in order, for our sake, to arrive.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c74_r1.htm_nts-sect74a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect74){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c75_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c75_r1.htm_page207}[\[VII\]](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c153_r1.htm_c153){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c75_r1.htm_c75 .chapter}

::: stanza
What silence around a god! How, inside it, you hear

every change in the sparkling fountain-spray

on the marble pool, as it leaps up and falls back entirely.

And over the laurel a feeling: three, perhaps four
:::

::: stanza
leaves that a butterfly touched. With a whir

it goes tumbling past, on the buoyant breath of the valley.

And now you remember another day

when you felt it, already so perfect, here,
:::

::: stanza
the silence around a god. But was it like this?

Isn't it spreading? Isn't it immense?

Isn't it pressing almost like a resistance
:::

::: stanza3
upon your resounding heart? Somewhere its beat is broken

on a soundless lull in the afternoon ...

There, He is.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c75_r1.htm_nts-sect75a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect75){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c76_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c76_r1.htm_page209}[\[VIII\]](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c154_r1.htm_c154){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c76_r1.htm_c76 .chapter}

::: stanza
We have overheard fountains all our days.

They sound to us almost like time.

But much more closely do they keep pace

with eternity's subtle rhythm.
:::

::: stanza
The water is strange and the water is yours,

from here and from far below.

You are the fountain-stone, unawares,

and all Things are mirrored in you.
:::

::: stanza
How distant this is, yet deeply akin,

long unriddled and never known,

senseless, then perfectly clear.
:::

::: stanza3
Your task is to love what you don't understand.

It grips your most secret emotion, and

rushes away with it. Where?
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c76_r1.htm_nts-sect76a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect76){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c77_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c77_r1.htm_page211}[\[IX\]](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c155_r1.htm_c155){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c77_r1.htm_c77 .chapter}

::: stanza
When was a *man* as awake

as this morning is?

Not just flower and brook:

the roof too rejoices.
:::

::: stanza
Even its weathered rim,

lit by the [sky---]{.nw}

finds it can feel: is home,

is answer, is day.
:::

::: stanza
Everything breathes in accord.

How tracelessly you have gone

away, you cares of the night.
:::

::: stanza3
Its darkness was formed,

in pure contradiction,

from legions of light.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c77_r1.htm_nts-sect77a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect77){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c78_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c78_r1.htm_page213}[\[FRAGMENTS\]](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c156_r1.htm_c156){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c78_r1.htm_c78 .chapter}

::: {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c78_r1.htm_pt1 .stanza}
\[i\]

Like held-in breath, serene and motionless

stands the nymph inside the ripening tree
:::

::: {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c78_r1.htm_pt2 .stanza}
\[ii\]

Look up. How calm the heavens are tonight.
:::

::: {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c78_r1.htm_pt3 .stanza}
\[iii\]

Lofty god of distant harmonies

I sense you everywhere deep in every Thing

upon the gently patterned slope the trees

stand silent as when first they heard you sing
:::

::: {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c78_r1.htm_pt4 .stanza}
\[iv\]

Mirror, you doppelgänger of space! O mirror, into you go

plunging the halves of smiles / perhaps the sweetest; for how

often the master's preliminary brushstroke, upon the

provisional page more fruitfully leaps up than, later,

the more controlled outline does on the ready background:

So do you, O unsayable presence, smile forth

your morning's descent and freedom into the ever-

accepting mirrors
:::

::: {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c78_r1.htm_pt5 .stanza}
\[v\]

Forever, O nymph, how long / I have marveled at you, amazed,

though you never stepped into my sight from out of the closed-in [tree---.]{.nw}

I am the time that is passing---you are the youngest age,

all that you asked from the gods has remained here, forever new.

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c78_r1.htm_page215}Yours is the meadow, even now it sways from the leap

with which you finally vanished into the elm.

Once, in the christian dawn. And our earliest hope:

for *your* sake isn't it planted into the springtime?
:::

::: stanza
Before we are moved by a girl, it is you that we think of
:::

::: {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c78_r1.htm_pt6 .stanza}
\[vi\]

.......... of the brown\
\

.......... on the sonorous

dried-up earth of the forest

[            ]{.poetryoffset}drums the flight of the faun
:::

::: {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c78_r1.htm_pt7 .stanza}
\[vii\]

This is the silent rising of the phalli
:::

::: {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c78_r1.htm_pt8 .stanza}
\[viii\]

About my answer: I still don't know

when I will bring it forth.

But listen, a harrow that already creates.

Up there in the vineyard someone, alone,

already speaks with the earth.
:::

::: {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c78_r1.htm_pt9 .stanza}
\[ix\]

Have you \[?ever observed\] the changing leaf-forms of the ivy
:::

::: {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c78_r1.htm_pt10 .stanza}
\[x\]

Protect yourself better

[        ]{.poetryoffset}protect yourself wanderer

with the road that is walking too
:::

::: {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c78_r1.htm_pt11 .stanza3}
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c78_r1.htm_page217}\[xi\]

Gather us now to hear love's legends.

Tell us of its daring, exquisite throes.

Where it was right, all things could be summoned;

here there are mostly abandoned vows.
:::

------------------------------------------------------------------------

::: note
[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c78_r1.htm_nts-sect78a}[Notes](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_nts_r1.htm_nts-sect78){.hlink}
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_p01a_r1.htm}

::: {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_p01a_r1.htm_p01a .part}
# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_p01a_r1.htm_pp123}*Duineser Elegien* {.part}

# *(1923)* {.part_title}

*Aus dem Besitz der Fuerstin Marie von Thurn und Taxis-Hohenlohe*\
*(1912/1922)*
:::

[]{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c79_r1.htm}

# []{#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c79_r1.htm_page2}[DIE ERSTE ELEGIE](#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c01_r1.htm){.hlink} {#Rilk_9780804153607_epub_c79_r1.htm_c79 .chapter}

::: stanza
Wer, wenn ich schriee, hörte mich denn aus der Engel

Ordnungen? und gesetzt selbst, es nähme

einer mich plötzlich ans Herz: ich verginge von seinem

stärkeren Dasein. Denn das Schöne ist nichts

als des Schrecklichen Anfang, den wir noch grade ertragen,

und wir bewundern es so, weil es gelassen verschmäht,

uns zu zerstören. Ein jeder Engel ist schrecklich.

[    ]{.poetryoffset}Und so verhalt ich mich denn und verschlucke den Lockruf

dunkelen Schluchzens. Ach, wen vermögen

wir denn zu brauchen? Engel nicht, Menschen nicht,

und die findigen Tiere merken es schon,

daß wir nicht sehr verläßlich zu Haus sind

in der gedeuteten Welt. Es bleibt uns vielleicht

irgend ein Baum an dem Abhang, daß wir ihn täglich

wiedersähen; es bleibt uns die Straße von gestern

und das verzogene Treusein einer Gewohnheit,

der es bei uns gefiel, und so blieb sie und ging nicht.

[    ]{.poetryoffset}O und die Nacht, die Nacht, wenn der Wind voller Weltraum

uns am Angesicht zehrt---, wem bliebe sie nicht, die ersehnte,

sanft enttäuschende, welche dem einzelnen Herzen

mühsam bevorsteht. Ist sie den Liebenden leichter?

Ach, sie verdecken sich nur mit einander ihr Los.

[    ]{.poetryoffset}Weißt du's *noch* nicht? Wirf aus den Armen die Leere

zu den Räumen hinzu, die wir atmen; vielleicht daß die Vögel

die erweiterte Luft fühlen mit innigerm Flug.
:::

::: stanza
Ja, die Frühlinge brauchten dich wohl. Es muteten manche

Sterne dir zu, daß du sie spürtest. Es hob

sich eine Woge heran im Vergangenen, oder

da du vorüberkamst am geöffneten Fenster,

gab eine Geige sich hin. Das alles war Auftrag.
